It sits between application code and the Kubernetes API server, abstracting both the complexity of HTTP serialization/deserialization and the low-level patterns needed for efficient resource watching.\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n- **k8s.io/apimachinery**: Core runtime types, serialization, watch events, errors\n- **k8s.io/api**: API type definitions (core v1, apps, batch, etc.)\n- **net/http**: Go standard library for HTTP transport\n- **context**: Go context for cancellation and deadlines\n\n### Downstream Consumers\n- Controllers (kube-controller-manager, kubelet, scheduler)\n- Client applications (kubectl, custom operators)\n- Testing frameworks and mock implementations\n- Plugin systems (auth providers, exec-based authentication)\n\n---\n\n## Core Components and Responsibility Boundaries\n\n### 1. REST Layer (`rest/` package)\n\n**Location**: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/rest/`\n\nThe REST layer provides low-level HTTP machinery that all higher-level clients ultimately use. It is responsible for:\n\n- **Config management** (`rest/config.go`): Holds connection parameters, authentication credentials, TLS settings, rate limits, and timeouts. The `Config` struct is the normalized in-memory representation of kubeconfig data, abstracting away file parsing concerns.\n\n- **Request building** (`rest/request.go`): Implements a fluent builder pattern for constructing Kubernetes API requests. Each request path element (verb, resource, namespace, etc.) is added via chained method calls like `.Get().Resource(\"pods\").Namespace(\"default\").Name(\"nginx\")`. This defers actual execution until a terminal method like `.Into(&obj)` is called.\n\n- **Transport layer** (`rest/transport.go`): Converts Config into a chain of `http.RoundTripper` middleware. Each middleware handles a specific concern: TLS certificate loading, bearer token injection, impersonation headers, basic auth, and per-request timeout enforcement.\n\n```go\n// Example Config fields (rest/config.go, lines 55-165)\ntype Config struct {\n    Host        string\n    APIPath     string\n    BearerToken string\n    QPS         float32     // Default 5.0\n    Burst       int         // Default 10\n    Transport   http.RoundTripper\n    WrapTransport transport.WrapperFunc\n    // ... auth, TLS, proxy, timeout fields\n}\n```\n\n**Key design decisions**:\n- Builder pattern separates request construction from execution, allowing code generation to produce type-safe wrappers without duplicating serialization logic\n- RoundTripper chain is the primary extension point for authentication and custom middleware\n- Content negotiation via Accept headers enables clients to request metadata-only objects (`as=PartialObjectMetadata`) or tables (`as=Table`), improving performance\n\n### 2. Typed Client (`kubernetes/` package)\n\n**Location**: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes/`\n\nThe Clientset provides compile-time type safety by grouping resources by API group and version. It is generated via `code-generator` from API type definitions.\n\n```go\n// kubernetes/clientset.go structure (lines 83-137)\ntype Interface interface {\n    Discovery() discovery.DiscoveryInterface\n    AppsV1() appsv1.AppsV1Interface\n    CoreV1() corev1.CoreV1Interface\n    BatchV1() batchv1.BatchV1Interface\n    // ... methods for all API groups and versions\n}\n\ntype Clientset struct {\n    *discovery.DiscoveryClient\n    appsV1        *appsv1.AppsV1Client\n    coreV1        *corev1.CoreV1Client\n    batchV1       *batchv1.BatchV1Client\n    // ... fields for all API groups\n}\n```\n\nEach group version interface (e.g., `AppsV1Interface`) provides access to a set of resource interfaces, each of which supports standard CRUD operations and subresources. For example:\n\n```go\n// Example usage pattern\nclientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"default\").Create(ctx, deployment, metav1.CreateOptions{})\nclientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"default\").Watch(ctx, metav1.ListOptions{})\n```\n\n**Responsibility**:\n- Presents strongly typed, method-based API for built-in resources\n- Encapsulates URL construction and serialization details\n- Enables static type checking and IDE autocomplete\n\n### 3. Dynamic Client (`dynamic/` package)\n\n**Location**: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/dynamic/`\n\nThe dynamic client handles resources unknown at compile time (notably CRDs) by representing all objects as `unstructured.Unstructured` (essentially a map of fields).\n\n```go\n// dynamic/interface.go (lines 29-50)\ntype Interface interface {\n    Resource(resource schema.GroupVersionResource) NamespaceableResourceInterface\n}\n\ntype ResourceInterface interface {\n    Create(ctx context.Context, obj *unstructured.Unstructured, ...) (*unstructured.Unstructured, error)\n    Get(ctx context.Context, name string, ...) (*unstructured.Unstructured, error)\n    List(ctx context.Context, opts metav1.ListOptions) (*unstructured.UnstructuredList, error)\n    Watch(ctx context.Context, opts metav1.ListOptions) (watch.Interface, error)\n    Patch(ctx context.Context, name string, pt types.PatchType, data []byte, ...) (*unstructured.Unstructured, error)\n}\n```\n\n**Coordination with discovery**:\nThe dynamic client depends on the `DiscoveryClient` to determine what resources exist and their API paths. Metadata about resource structure comes from OpenAPI schemas fetched from `/openapi/v3`.\n\n### 4. Discovery Client (`discovery/` package)\n\n**Location**: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/discovery/`\n\nThe discovery client introspects the API server to learn what API groups, versions, and resources it supports. This is essential for dynamic clients and tools like kubectl.\n\n**Key interfaces** (`discovery/discovery_client.go`, lines 77-155):\n\n```go\ntype DiscoveryInterface interface {\n    RESTClient() restclient.Interface\n    ServerGroupsInterface\n    ServerResourcesInterface\n    ServerVersionInterface\n    OpenAPISchemaInterface\n    OpenAPIV3SchemaInterface\n    WithLegacy() DiscoveryInterface\n}\n\ntype ServerResourcesInterface interface {\n    ServerResourcesForGroupVersion(groupVersion string) (*metav1.APIResourceList, error)\n    ServerGroupsAndResources() ([]*metav1.APIGroup, []*metav1.APIResourceList, error)\n    ServerPreferredResources() ([]*metav1.APIResourceList, error)\n}\n```\n\n**Aggregated discovery** (v2 format): Recent versions support `/api/v1/groups` endpoint returning `APIGroupDiscoveryList`, which combines groups and resources in a single request, reducing overhead.\n\n**CachedDiscoveryClient**: A wrapper that disk-caches discovery data (by default in `~/.kube/cache/discovery/`), improving startup time. The cache must be explicitly invalidated via `.Invalidate()` if stale data is detected.\n\n### 5. Informer Machinery (`tools/cache/` package)\n\n**Location**: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/`\n\nThe informer is the core of client-go's event-driven architecture. It replaces a polling-heavy pattern with an efficient, cached, watch-based model.\n\n#### 5.1 Reflector (`tools/cache/reflector.go`)\n\nThe reflector is the bridge between the API server and the local cache. It performs two operations in sequence:\n\n1. **Initial LIST**: Fetches all objects of a resource type, capturing the `resourceVersion` at that moment\n2. **Continuous WATCH**: Streams changes from that `resourceVersion` forward\n\n```go\n// reflector.go (lines 87-148)\ntype Reflector struct {\n    name            string\n    expectedType    reflect.Type\n    store           ReflectorStore       // Receives updates\n    listerWatcher   ListerWatcherWithContext\n    resyncPeriod    time.Duration\n    lastSyncResourceVersion string\n    // ...\n}\n\nfunc (r *Reflector) ListAndWatchWithContext(ctx context.Context) error {\n    // Either watchList or traditional list+watch\n    if r.useWatchList {\n        w, err = r.watchList(ctx)\n        // ...\n    } else {\n        err = r.list(ctx)\n        // ...\n    }\n    return r.watchWithResync(ctx, w)\n}\n```\n\n**Resilience mechanisms**:\n- **Exponential backoff** on watch failures (800ms initial, up to 30s)\n- **Watch bookmarks**: Server-sent bookmark events provide updated `resourceVersion` when the connection is stale, allowing recovery without full re-list\n- **\"Too old\" resource version handling**: If a WATCH fails because the requested `resourceVersion` is too old (server-side history window exceeded), the reflector automatically re-lists and resumes watching\n- **Resync**: Periodic full-cache traversal (configurable via `resyncPeriod`) to catch mutations the watch stream may have missed due to server-side crashes or network partitions\n\n#### 5.2 DeltaFIFO (`tools/cache/delta_fifo.go`)\n\nBuffers changes before they reach the cache, preserving ordering and deduplication semantics. Each item in the FIFO is associated with a slice of `DeltaType` events (Added, Modified, Deleted, Sync). If an object is modified multiple times before being popped, only the final state is forwarded to the cache.\n\n#### 5.3 Indexer (Thread-Safe Store) (`tools/cache/store.go`, `tools/cache/index.go`)\n\nThe indexer is the in-process cache. It stores objects keyed by namespace and name (e.g., `\"default/nginx\"`), and supports secondary indices for efficient lookups (e.g., by owner reference or label).\n\n```go\n// tools/cache/listers.go (lines 1-50)\n// Lister is the thread-safe, read-only interface to the cache\ntype Lister interface {\n    List(selector labels.Selector) (ret []interface{}, err error)\n    Get(name string) (ret interface{}, err error)\n}\n```\n\n#### 5.4 SharedInformer (`tools/cache/shared_informer.go`)\n\nMultiplexes a single Reflector+DeltaFIFO+Indexer across many event handler subscribers. Without SharedInformer, each handler would need its own watch stream, overwhelming the API server.\n\n```go\n// tools/cache/shared_informer.go (lines 140-150)\ntype SharedInformer interface {\n    AddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\n    GetStore() Store\n    GetIndexer() Indexer\n    Run(stopCh <-chan struct{})\n    HasSynced() bool\n}\n\n// ResourceEventHandler receives cache events\ntype ResourceEventHandler interface {\n    OnAdd(obj interface{}, isInitialList bool)\n    OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{})\n    OnDelete(obj interface{})\n}\n```\n\nEvent handlers are called in order, sequentially, **after** the cache has been updated. This ordering is critical for controller correctness: handlers never see stale cache data.\n\n#### 5.5 Informer Factory (`informers/factory.go`)\n\nFactory that creates and manages a family of typed SharedInformers for a single Clientset. Ensures each resource type has at most one Reflector, reducing API server load.\n\n```go\n// informers/factory.go (lines 54-112)\ntype SharedInformerFactory interface {\n    Start(stopCh <-chan struct{})\n    WaitForCacheSync(stopCh <-chan struct{}) map[reflect.Type]bool\n    Apps() apps.Interface      // Provides AppV1(), AppV1beta1(), etc.\n    Batch() batch.Interface\n    Core() core.Interface\n    // ...\n}\n\nfunc NewSharedInformerFactoryWithOptions(\n    client kubernetes.Interface,\n    defaultResync time.Duration,\n    options ...SharedInformerOption,\n) SharedInformerFactory {\n    // Supports WithNamespace(), WithTweakListOptions(), WithCustomResyncConfig(), WithTransform()\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## End-to-End Control Flow: From Event to Reconciliation\n\n### Scenario: A Deployment is updated\n\n```\nAPI Server (persistent state)\n    ↓\n[1] Reflector.watchList() or list() + watch()\n    ↓\n[2] Watch event (MODIFIED) streamed to reflector\n    ↓\n[3] Reflector sends object to DeltaFIFO.Add()\n    ↓\n[4] DeltaFIFO internal goroutine pops item, sends to Indexer\n    ↓\n[5] Indexer updates cache, calls SharedInformer.OnUpdate()\n    ↓\n[6] SharedInformer dispatches to registered event handlers\n    ↓\n[7] Event handler calls: workqueue.Add(\"deployment/default/my-deploy\")\n    ↓\n[8] Controller.Run() calls: item, _ := workqueue.Get()\n    ↓\n[9] Controller reconcile loop:\n    - Fetch from cache: lister.Get(\"default/my-deploy\")\n    - Perform business logic (e.g., check replica count)\n    - Issue API calls if needed (e.g., patch status)\n    - workqueue.Done(item)\n    ↓\n[10] If error, workqueue re-enqueues with exponential backoff\n```\n\n### File evidence of flow:\n\n1. **Reflector start**: `tools/cache/reflector.go:364-373` (`RunWithContext`)\n2. **List and watch**: `tools/cache/reflector.go:408-447` (`ListAndWatchWithContext`)\n3. **Watch stream handling**: `tools/cache/reflector.go:499-700+` (`watch()` method processes events)\n4. **DeltaFIFO queuing**: `tools/cache/delta_fifo.go` (internal Add/Update/Delete feed the FIFO)\n5. **Indexer update**: `tools/cache/store.go` (cache population after FIFO pops)\n6. **Event handler dispatch**: `tools/cache/shared_informer.go` (processor listeners triggered post-cache-update)\n7. **Work queue integration**: `util/workqueue/queue.go:30-52` (TypedInterface for Add/Get/Done)\n\n### Code Generation Integration\n\nTyped informers and listers are generated via `k8s.io/code-generator`. The generation process creates:\n- **Typed Clientsets** (e.g., `kubernetes.Clientset`)\n- **Typed Informers** (e.g., `v1.PodInformer`)\n- **Typed Listers** (e.g., `v1.PodLister`) — read-only cache accessors\n- **Apply configurations** (e.g., `v1.DeploymentApplyConfiguration`) for Server-Side Apply\n\nFor the Kubernetes repository itself, code generation is invoked via `hack/update-codegen.sh`.\n\n---\n\n## Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 1. Watch Stream Disconnection\n\n**Symptom**: Reflector logs \"Failed to watch\" or \"error(conn-refused)\"\n\n**Recovery**:\n- Exponential backoff triggers `ListAndWatch` again\n- Full re-list ensures no gap in cache (though potentially stale)\n- Watch bookmarks (if supported) help resume from a recent resourceVersion without full re-list\n\n**Tradeoff**: Re-listing on every watch failure is expensive but guarantees eventual consistency. Without it, the cache could permanently miss objects.\n\n### 2. Resource Version Too Old\n\n**Symptom**: Watch fails with `410 Gone` (resource version expired on server)\n\n**Cause**: Etcd history (default 5 minutes) has been garbage collected; the client's cached `resourceVersion` is too old.\n\n**Recovery** (`reflector.go:120-122`):\n```go\nisLastSyncResourceVersionUnavailable bool  // Set to true on 410 error\n```\nNext `ListAndWatch` cycle performs a full re-list to get a current resource version.\n\n**Limit**: If a controller is paused for longer than the server's history window, it **will** miss intermediate states. Controllers should be designed to be idempotent and re-reconcile all objects periodically (via resync).\n\n### 3. Event Handler Blocking\n\n**Symptom**: Watch stream stalls, reflector unable to process events\n\n**Root cause**: Event handler (or downstream workqueue) blocks, holding the lock in `SharedInformer`.\n\n**Mitigation** (`tools/cache/shared_informer.go:131-135`):\n- Event handlers must complete quickly\n- Long-running work should be delegated to a workqueue consumer\n- Handlers run sequentially; blocking one handler blocks all others for the same informer\n\n**Best practice**: Handlers should only call `workqueue.Add(key)` and return immediately.\n\n### 4. High-Frequency Resync\n\n**Symptom**: CPU spike, API server load spike\n\n**Cause**: `resyncPeriod` is too small (e.g., 1 second instead of the default 0 or 30s).\n\n**Impact**:\n- Full cache traverse every N seconds\n- Calls `Indexer.Resync()` which re-triggers all event handlers\n- Can be amplified across many controllers\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Use sensible defaults (0 = no resync, or 30s+ for slow-changing resources)\n- Set via `informers/factory.go:77-85` (`WithCustomResyncConfig`)\n\n### 5. List Pagination and Consistency\n\n**Feature** (Reflector `WatchListPageSize`):\n- Paginated LIST requests (configurable chunk size) reduce per-request memory on both client and server\n- **Design tradeoff**: Paginated lists are served directly from etcd, bypassing cache, so they are slower than watch cache serves\n\n**Default behavior**:\n- Consistent reads (RV=\"\") or old reads (RV=\"0\"): uses paging\n- Specific resourceVersion reads: disables pagination to use watch cache\n\n### 6. Server-Side vs. Client-Side Rate Limiting\n\n**Client-side rate limiting** (`rest/config.go:117-129`):\n- `QPS` (default 5.0) and `Burst` (default 10) control client's token bucket\n- Prevents overwhelming the server\n\n**Server-side rate limiting** (API Priority and Fairness):\n- Server enforces priority classes and flow control\n- Client handles HTTP 429 with exponential backoff (Retry-After header)\n\n**Interaction**:\n- If client-side QPS/Burst are too high, server will throttle and client will backoff\n- If too low, workload is unnecessarily slow\n- Default values are conservative; set based on actual workload and API server capacity\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 1. Custom Transport Middleware\n\n**Location**: `rest/config.go` and `rest/transport.go`\n\n```go\nconfig := &rest.Config{\n    Host: \"https://...\",\n    // ... auth, TLS, etc.\n    WrapTransport: func(rt http.RoundTripper) http.RoundTripper {\n        return &customMiddleware{rt: rt}\n    },\n}\n```\n\nUse cases:\n- Request/response logging and tracing\n- Custom retry logic or circuit breaking\n- Request header injection (e.g., tracing context, custom authentication)\n- Rate limiting per endpoint\n\n**Risk**: Broken middleware can cause all API calls to fail silently. Test thoroughly.\n\n### 2. Custom ListerWatcher\n\n**Location**: `tools/cache/reflector.go:104-105`\n\n```go\nlw := &cache.ListWatch{\n    ListFunc: func(options metav1.ListOptions) (runtime.Object, error) {\n        // Custom list logic, e.g., from cache, database, or filtered API call\n    },\n    WatchFunc: func(options metav1.ListOptions) (watch.Interface, error) {\n        // Custom watch, e.g., synthetic watch from polling\n    },\n}\n\nreflector := cache.NewReflector(lw, &v1.Pod{}, store, resyncPeriod)\n```\n\nUse cases:\n- **Filtering at source**: Reduce cache size by pre-filtering in ListFunc\n- **Non-API sources**: Watch resources stored in a database or cache\n- **Test mocks**: Deterministic watch streams for testing controller logic\n\n**Risk**: If ListFunc and WatchFunc are inconsistent, the cache can drift from truth. Ensure both serve the same semantics.\n\n### 3. Custom Indexers\n\n**Location**: `tools/cache/index.go`\n\n```go\nindexers := cache.Indexers{\n    cache.NamespaceIndex: cache.MetaNamespaceIndexFunc,\n    \"byOwnerRef\": func(obj interface{}) ([]string, error) {\n        pod := obj.(*v1.Pod)\n        var owners []string\n        for _, ref := range pod.OwnerReferences {\n            owners = append(owners, ref.UID)\n        }\n        return owners, nil\n    },\n}\nindexer := cache.NewIndexer(cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc, indexers)\n```\n\nUse cases:\n- Fast lookups by non-primary attributes (e.g., by owner, by label, by field)\n- Reduces O(n) scans to indexed lookups\n\n**Trade-off**: Index maintenance overhead vs. lookup speed. Most applications only need the default namespace/name index.\n\n### 4. Transform Function on Cache Items\n\n**Location**: `informers/factory.go:103-109` (`WithTransform`)\n\n```go\nfactory := informers.NewSharedInformerFactoryWithOptions(\n    client, 30*time.Second,\n    informers.WithTransform(func(obj interface{}) (interface{}, error) {\n        pod := obj.(*v1.Pod)\n        // Remove sensitive fields, apply annotations, etc.\n        return pod, nil\n    }),\n)\n```\n\nUse case:\n- Strip sensitive data before storing in cache\n- Normalize objects on ingestion\n\n**Risk**: If transform is lossy, controllers cannot recover the original data.\n\n### 5. Custom Event Handler with Lifecycle Hooks\n\n**Location**: `tools/cache/shared_informer.go:150-180`\n\n```go\ntype ResourceEventHandlerFuncs struct {\n    AddFunc    func(obj interface{}, isInitialList bool)\n    UpdateFunc func(oldObj, newObj interface{})\n    DeleteFunc func(obj interface{})\n}\n\n// Or use AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod for per-handler resync\ninformer.AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod(\n    &ResourceEventHandlerFuncs{\n        AddFunc: func(obj interface{}, _ bool) { workqueue.Add(keyOf(obj)) },\n        UpdateFunc: func(_, newObj interface{}) { workqueue.Add(keyOf(newObj)) },\n        DeleteFunc: func(obj interface{}) { workqueue.Add(keyOf(obj)) },\n    },\n    30*time.Second, // per-handler resync (if non-zero)\n)\n```\n\n**Lifecycle semantics**:\n- `isInitialList=true` on initial sync, `false` on all subsequent updates\n- Delete notifications carry the **last known state** (except resourceVersion is updated to reflect deletion)\n- Sequential delivery: one handler's output doesn't run until previous handlers finish\n\n### 6. Server-Side Apply Configuration (Declarative Patching)\n\n**Location**: `applyconfigurations/` (generated), `util/apply/` package\n\n```go\n// Instead of get-modify-update:\ndeployment := applyconfigurations.Deployment(\"default\", \"my-deploy\").\n    WithSpec(applyconfigurations.DeploymentSpec().\n        WithReplicas(3).\n        WithSelector(...))\n\nresult, err := clientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"default\").\n    Apply(ctx, deployment, metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: \"my-controller\"})\n```\n\n**Advantages**:\n- Multiple controllers can safely co-manage the same object (via field ownership)\n- No race conditions between get and update\n- Server handles conflict resolution\n\n**Extension point**: Field managers are arbitrary strings; controllers declare ownership by FieldManager name.\n\n### 7. AuthProvider and ExecProvider Plugins\n\n**Location**: `rest/config.go:85-92`, `rest/plugin.go`\n\n```go\nconfig := &rest.Config{\n    // ...\n    AuthProvider: &clientcmdapi.AuthProviderConfig{\n        Name: \"oidc\",\n        Config: map[string]string{\n            \"client-id\": \"...\",\n            \"client-secret\": \"...\",\n        },\n    },\n}\n\n// Or use exec-based auth\nconfig.ExecProvider = &clientcmdapi.ExecConfig{\n    APIVersion: \"client.authentication.k8s.io/v1\",\n    Command: \"/path/to/auth-script\",\n}\n```\n\n**Lifecycle**:\n- Auth providers are loaded lazily on first API call\n- ExecProvider is invoked per-request if token is expired\n- WrapTransport is the mechanism for injecting auth headers\n\n**Extension paths**: Custom implementations via plugin interface.\n\n### 8. Custom Rate Limiter\n\n**Location**: `util/flowcontrol/`, `rest/config.go:128-129`\n\n```go\nimport \"k8s.io/client-go/util/flowcontrol\"\n\nlimiter := flowcontrol.NewTokenBucketRateLimiter(100, 10)\nconfig := &rest.Config{\n    // ...\n    RateLimiter: limiter,\n}\n```\n\nUse cases:\n- Adaptive rate limiting based on server response codes\n- Per-endpoint rate limits\n- Jitter to prevent thundering herd\n\n---\n\n## Operational Implications and Performance Considerations\n\n### 1. Memory Footprint\n\n**Cache Size**: Directly proportional to number of resources of each watched type.\n\n**Estimation**:\n- Typical Pod object: ~1-2 KB in memory\n- 10,000 Pods × 2 KB = ~20 MB cache\n- Add informer overhead (indices, event queues): 30-40 MB total\n\n**Optimization**:\n- Watch only needed resources (use `WithTweakListOptions` to filter)\n- Use `WithTransform` to strip large fields (e.g., logs, raw data)\n- Use metadata-only informer (`PartialObjectMetadata`) when full objects aren't needed\n\n### 2. API Server Load\n\n**Watch streams**: Each SharedInformer opens one WATCH request per resource type. With 10 controllers on a cluster, you have 10 Deployments watchers = 10 watch streams on the server.\n\n**Reflector resync**: Periodic full-cache traversal. If set too aggressively across many controllers, can spike API server CPU.\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Use SharedInformerFactory to share watchers across controllers\n- Set resync periods appropriately (default 0 or 30s+, not 1s)\n- Monitor watch stream count: `kube-apiserver_watch_cache_*` metrics\n\n### 3. Network Efficiency\n\n**Watch bookmarks** (`reflector.go:127-128`): Enable via feature gate `WatchListClient`. Reduces reconnection overhead by providing a recent resourceVersion on bookmark events.\n\n**List pagination** (`reflector.go:127-134`): Reduces per-request size on initial sync. Trade-off: slightly slower (served from etcd, not watch cache).\n\n**Protobuf encoding**:\n- Default JSON is ~1.5x larger than Protobuf\n- For high-volume scenarios (many objects, high QPS), consider `--prefers-protobuf` flag on generated clients\n\n### 4. CPU and GC Pressure\n\n**Reflector event processing**:\n- Allocates event objects per watch message\n- DeltaFIFO maintains linked list of deltas\n- Indexer maintains multiple indices\n\n**GC optimization**:\n- Ensure resync periods are not too aggressive\n- Limit cache size via filtering\n- Monitor heap profiling: `pprof /debug/pprof/heap`\n\n### 5. Latency: From Event to Controller Action\n\n**Typical end-to-end latency**:\n1. Object mutation on API server: 0 ms (reference point)\n2. WATCH stream delivery: 1-100 ms (network + serialization)\n3. Reflector processing: 1-10 ms\n4. DeltaFIFO → Indexer: <1 ms\n5. Event handler dispatch → workqueue.Add: <1 ms\n6. workqueue.Get: 0-1 ms (already queued)\n7. Controller reconcile: 10 ms - seconds (business logic)\n\n**Total**: Typically 20-100 ms from mutation to workqueue entry, assuming no backpressure.\n\n**Bottlenecks**:\n- Event handler blocking (blocks all handlers for that informer)\n- Workqueue consumer paused or slow (events accumulate)\n- Watch stream dropped (forces full re-list, expensive)\n\n### 6. Multi-Controller Scaling\n\n**Shared discovery cache**: Only one `CachedDiscoveryClient` is needed per kube-config. Multiple controllers can share it.\n\n**Shared informer factory**: Critical for efficiency. All controllers using the same SharedInformerFactory share a single Reflector per resource type.\n\n**Separate client vs. shared informer factory**:\n```go\n// Inefficient: two separate factories, two watch streams for Pods\nfactory1 := informers.NewSharedInformerFactory(clientset, 30*time.Second)\nfactory2 := informers.NewSharedInformerFactory(clientset, 30*time.Second)\npodInformer1 := factory1.Core().V1().Pods() // watch stream 1\npodInformer2 := factory2.Core().V1().Pods() // watch stream 2\n\n// Efficient: shared factory\nfactory := informers.NewSharedInformerFactory(clientset, 30*time.Second)\npodInformer1 := factory.Core().V1().Pods()  // same watch stream\npodInformer2 := factory.Core().V1().Pods()  // same watch stream\n```\n\n---\n\n## Important Files and Directory Map\n\n### Core REST and Transport\n- `rest/config.go` — Configuration struct and defaults\n- `rest/request.go` — Request builder and execution\n- `rest/transport.go` — Transport chain construction\n- `rest/with_retry.go` — Retry logic and backoff\n- `rest/warnings.go` — Warning header handling\n\n### Typed Clients\n- `kubernetes/clientset.go` — Generated Clientset struct\n- `kubernetes/typed/*/v1/client.go` — Typed client implementations (e.g., `typed/apps/v1/deployment.go`)\n\n### Dynamic Client\n- `dynamic/interface.go` — Dynamic client interfaces\n- `dynamic/simple.go` — Implementation using unstructured objects\n\n### Discovery\n- `discovery/discovery_client.go` — DiscoveryClient interface and implementation\n- `discovery/cached/` — CachedDiscoveryClient implementation\n- `discovery/helper.go` — Utility functions for discovery results\n\n### Informers and Cache\n- `tools/cache/reflector.go` — Reflector: LIST + WATCH + resync\n- `tools/cache/delta_fifo.go` — Delta FIFO queue\n- `tools/cache/store.go` — Cache store interface and default implementation\n- `tools/cache/index.go` — Indexing and secondary indices\n- `tools/cache/shared_informer.go` — SharedInformer: event multiplexing\n- `tools/cache/listers.go` — Generated lister interfaces (read-only cache accessors)\n\n### Informer Factory\n- `informers/factory.go` — SharedInformerFactory, coordinates all informers\n\n### Work Queue and Synchronization\n- `util/workqueue/queue.go` — Work queue interface and FIFO implementation\n- `util/workqueue/delaying_queue.go` — Delayed queue (for exponential backoff)\n- `util/workqueue/rate_limiting_queue.go` — Rate-limited queue (combines delaying + rate limiting)\n- `util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go` — Built-in rate limiters (exponential, linear backoff)\n\n### Tools and Utilities\n- `tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go` — Leader election machinery\n- `tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/` — Lock implementations (Lease, ConfigMap, etc.)\n- `tools/clientcmd/` — Kubeconfig parsing and client construction\n- `util/flowcontrol/` — Token bucket rate limiting\n\n### Code Generation\n- Referenced but not in client-go repo: `k8s.io/code-generator/` (external)\n- Output: clientset, informers, listers, apply configurations\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nClient-go's architecture achieves its goal of providing both ergonomic (typed client) and powerful (dynamic, watch-based, cached) interfaces to the Kubernetes API by layering abstractions:\n\n1. **REST layer**: Generic HTTP request builder with middleware chain for auth and transport\n2. **Typed and dynamic clients**: Build on REST layer, differing only in serialization strategy\n3. **Discovery**: Runtime introspection of API server capabilities\n4. **Informer machinery**: Event-driven caching with careful handling of watch disconnections, resource version expiry, and eventual consistency\n5. **Work queue and factories**: Coordinate multiple consumers of the same watch stream\n\nThe design emphasizes **resilience** (exponential backoff, bookmarks, re-sync), **efficiency** (single watch per resource type, cached reads), and **extensibility** (custom transport, ListerWatcher, indices, rate limiters). Controllers built with this library can scale from a single process to thousands of controllers per cluster without re-engineering the underlying machinery.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
